  ID: 3458764662578407045
  Type: sticky_note (sticky)
  Content: 1. While the application is pending and Leon remains overseas, can he continue contracting for a different non-UK group entity? SRA – Yes, Leon can continue contracting for a different non-UK group entity until the time Couch Heroes UK decides they are ready to sponsor Leon.  He can continue to work for a different entity until the date he arrives in the UK on his Skilled Worker visa to start work for Couch Heroes UK. 2. Once the work permit is granted but before the UK employment start date, can that contractor engagement continue, and does it matter whether he's already entered the UK or not? SRA – Once Leon has entered the UK on his Skilled Worker visa, he must then be working full time for Couch Heroes UK and must not continue his contracted work for the overseas entity.  Under his Skilled Worker visa Leon will be allowed to work up to 20 hours per week for a different entity (in the UK or outside the UK) provided his main sponsored work in the UK is not affected and these additional 20 hours of work he does is after he has completed his work obligations with his UK sponsor (Couch Heroes UK).  For e.g.  – if Leon wanted to benefit from the 20 hours per week allowance and work for a different entity, so long as he works in the evenings (after his UK sponsored working hours) or weekends that will be fine. This does not have to be reported to the Home Office, but Leon must ensure that he does not work for more than 20 hours per week.  The Home Office can check the National Insurance UK data for Leon and where they find he is earning an unusually high income while present in the UK, which does not tally with his UK sponsorship with Couch Heroes UK, they can at any time query his earning. 3. Any other strict requirements for stopping work whilst the application is pending or after it has been approved we should be aware of? SRA – Where an individual is making a Skilled Worker application from overseas to come to the UK to work, there are no restrictions or conditions regarding their ability to continue their work arrangement overseas.  The Home Office does not question what their work activity has been overseas (whether it is employment or self-employment).  It is once the individual arrives in the UK on their Skilled Worker visa that the immigration conditions come into effect and the individual must then continue to adhere to the immigration conditions until the date their UK sponsorship ends and they return overseas,  or  if they become a settled status holder in the UK. In contrast however, an individual who is already in the UK as a Skilled Worker or on a different immigration category, they have to follow certain conditions on when they can start work with a different sponsor.   For e.g.  - a person who is already sponsored in the UK cannot start working for their new sponsor on a full-time basis if the new sponsorship visa has not been approved, or if their notice period / garden leave with the original sponsor has not ended.

  Content: 1. While the application is pending and Leon remains overseas, can he continue contracting for a different non-UK group entity? SRA – Yes, Leon can continue contracting for a different non-UK group entity until the time Couch Heroes UK decides they are ready to sponsor Leon.  He can continue to work for a different entity until the date he arrives in the UK on his Skilled Worker visa to start work for Couch Heroes UK. 2. Once the work permit is granted but before the UK employment start date, can that contractor engagement continue, and does it matter whether he's already entered the UK or not? SRA – Once Leon has entered the UK on his Skilled Worker visa, he must then be working full time for Couch Heroes UK and must not continue his contracted work for the overseas entity.  Under his Skilled Worker visa Leon will be allowed to work up to 20 hours per week for a different entity (in the UK or outside the UK) provided his main sponsored work in the UK is not affected and these additional 20 hours of work he does is after he has completed his work obligations with his UK sponsor (Couch Heroes UK).  For e.g.  – if Leon wanted to benefit from the 20 hours per week allowance and work for a different entity, so long as he works in the evenings (after his UK sponsored working hours) or weekends that will be fine. This does not have to be reported to the Home Office, but Leon must ensure that he does not work for more than 20 hours per week.  The Home Office can check the National Insurance UK data for Leon and where they find he is earning an unusually high income while present in the UK, which does not tally with his UK sponsorship with Couch Heroes UK, they can at any time query his earning. 3. Any other strict requirements for stopping work whilst the application is pending or after it has been approved we should be aware of? SRA – Where an individual is making a Skilled Worker application from overseas to come to the UK to work, there are no restrictions or conditions regarding their ability to continue their work arrangement overseas.  The Home Office does not question what their work activity has been overseas (whether it is employment or self-employment).  It is once the individual arrives in the UK on their Skilled Worker visa that the immigration conditions come into effect and the individual must then continue to adhere to the immigration conditions until the date their UK sponsorship ends and they return overseas,  or  if they become a settled status holder in the UK. In contrast however, an individual who is already in the UK as a Skilled Worker or on a different immigration category, they have to follow certain conditions on when they can start work with a different sponsor.   For e.g.  - a person who is already sponsored in the UK cannot start working for their new sponsor on a full-time basis if the new sponsorship visa has not been approved, or if their notice period / garden leave with the original sponsor has not ended.

SECTION 4: MATCHED RESULTS - NUMERIC ITEMS TO FEATURES
(145 matches found)
========================================================================================================================

  FEATURE: 1. While the application is pending and Leon remains overseas, can he continue contracting for a different non-UK group entity? SRA – Yes, Leon can continue contracting for a different non-UK group entity until the time Couch Heroes UK decides they are ready to sponsor Leon.  He can continue to work for a different entity until the date he arrives in the UK on his Skilled Worker visa to start work for Couch Heroes UK. 2. Once the work permit is granted but before the UK employment start date, can that contractor engagement continue, and does it matter whether he's already entered the UK or not? SRA – Once Leon has entered the UK on his Skilled Worker visa, he must then be working full time for Couch Heroes UK and must not continue his contracted work for the overseas entity.  Under his Skilled Worker visa Leon will be allowed to work up to 20 hours per week for a different entity (in the UK or outside the UK) provided his main sponsored work in the UK is not affected and these additional 20 hours of work he does is after he has completed his work obligations with his UK sponsor (Couch Heroes UK).  For e.g.  – if Leon wanted to benefit from the 20 hours per week allowance and work for a different entity, so long as he works in the evenings (after his UK sponsored working hours) or weekends that will be fine. This does not have to be reported to the Home Office, but Leon must ensure that he does not work for more than 20 hours per week.  The Home Office can check the National Insurance UK data for Leon and where they find he is earning an unusually high income while present in the UK, which does not tally with his UK sponsorship with Couch Heroes UK, they can at any time query his earning. 3. Any other strict requirements for stopping work whilst the application is pending or after it has been approved we should be aware of? SRA – Where an individual is making a Skilled Worker application from overseas to come to the UK to work, there are no restrictions or conditions regarding their ability to continue their work arrangement overseas.  The Home Office does not question what their work activity has been overseas (whether it is employment or self-employment).  It is once the individual arrives in the UK on their Skilled Worker visa that the immigration conditions come into effect and the individual must then continue to adhere to the immigration conditions until the date their UK sponsorship ends and they return overseas,  or  if they become a settled status holder in the UK. In contrast however, an individual who is already in the UK as a Skilled Worker or on a different immigration category, they have to follow certain conditions on when they can start work with a different sponsor.   For e.g.  - a person who is already sponsored in the UK cannot start working for their new sponsor on a full-time basis if the new sponsorship visa has not been approved, or if their notice period / garden leave with the original sponsor has not ended.

SRA – Once Leon has entered the UK on his Skilled Worker visa, he must then be working full time for Couch Heroes UK and must not continue his contracted work for the overseas entity.  Under his Skilled Worker visa Leon will be allowed to work up to 20 hours per week for a different entity (in the UK or outside the UK) provided his main sponsored work in the UK is not affected and these additional 20 hours of work he does is after he has completed his work obligations with his UK sponsor (Couch Heroes UK).  For e.g.  – if Leon wanted to benefit from the 20 hours per week allowance and work for a different entity, so long as he works in the evenings (after his UK sponsored working hours) or weekends that will be fine. This does not have to be reported to the Home Office, but Leon must ensure that he does not work for more than 20 hours per week.  The Home Office can check the National Insurance UK data for Leon and where they find he is earning an unusually high income while present in the UK, which does not tally with his UK sponsorship with Couch Heroes UK, they can at any time query his earning. 3. Any other strict requirements for stopping work whilst the application is pending or after it has been approved we should be aware of? SRA – Where an individual is making a Skilled Worker application from overseas to come to the UK to work, there are no restrictions or conditions regarding their ability to continue their work arrangement overseas.  The Home Office does not question what their work activity has been overseas (whether it is employment or self-employment).  It is once the individual arrives in the UK on their Skilled Worker visa that the immigration conditions come into effect and the individual must then continue to adhere to the immigration conditions until the date their UK sponsorship ends and they return overseas,  or  if they become a settled status holder in the UK. In contrast however, an individual who is already in the UK as a Skilled Worker or on a different immigration category, they have to follow certain conditions on when they can start work with a different sponsor.   For e.g.  - a person who is already sponsored in the UK cannot start working for their new sponsor on a full-time basis if the new sponsorship visa has not been approved, or if their notice period / garden leave with the original sponsor has not ended."

  Content: Right to Work Checks – Existing Staff All evidence relating to existing employees must be in place before the licence application is submitted. Conduct checks now for anyone not yet verified. For British/Irish Citizens (Manual Check) •       See the original passport •       Make a clear copy that cannot be manually altered •       Annotate the copy (see below) For Non-British/Irish Staff (Online Check) •       Use the Home Office online checking service with their share code •        Do NOT accept physical BRC, BRP or Frontier Work Permits  – these must now be checked via eVisa •       Retain the 'profile' page confirming right to work Personnel File Contents Each employee file should include (at minimum): •       Annotated right to work document copies (separate, clearly identifiable section) •       Current passport page copies (personal details, visas, immigration stamps) •       Document showing National Insurance number •       Current contact details (address, phone, mobile, emergency contact) •         Historical   contact details (do not overwrite – keep a dated record of changes) •       Signed contract of employment •       Job description •       Payslips or capability to print them at short notice •       Absence record (distinguishing annual leave, sick, compassionate, unauthorised) •       Copies of qualifications, registrations, and professional accreditations •       Pre-employment references Systems to Implement •        Foreign national register:  All foreign national employees (sponsored or not) with job title, immigration status, sponsorship status, and working location •        Visa expiry tracker:  Monitor leave to enter/remain expiry dates and flag repeat checks •        Absence reporting process:  Must flag 10+ consecutive days of unauthorised absence for reporting to Home Office within 10 working days •        Contact details update process:  Quarterly or half-yearly reminder for sponsored employees to confirm/update details •        Hierarchy chart:  Showing where each sponsored migrant fits in the organisation •        Professional registration tracker:  Monitor expiry dates of any required registrations/accreditations Storage Requirements •       Files can be electronic, hard copy, or a combination •       Must be well organised with consistent structure across all files •       Must be kept securely (locked cabinet or password-protected) •       Backup system should be in place •       Accessible at the office at all times and retrievable promptly •       Retain for duration of employment + 2 years, then securely destroy we need to check with Saud regarding annotation system and most importantly whether the employment-specific requirements apply to uk-based contractors as well (i think it does based on research and previous discussions) [HAS NUMBER]
